				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coca-Cola_Company&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Coca-Cola Company">Coca-Cola Company</a>)</span></div>
			</div>
			
			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the company. For the carbonated beverage, see <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a>.</div>

<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<p><b>The Coca-Cola Company</b> is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporation</a>, and manufacturer, retailer, and marketer of nonalcoholic beverage concentrates and <a href="/wiki/Syrup" title="Syrup">syrups</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> The company produces <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a>, invented in 1886 by pharmacist <a href="/wiki/John_Stith_Pemberton" title="John Stith Pemberton">John Stith Pemberton</a> in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> In 1889 the formula and brand were sold for $2,300 to <a href="/wiki/Asa_Griggs_Candler" title="Asa Griggs Candler">Asa Griggs Candler</a>, who incorporated The Coca-Cola Company in Atlanta in 1892.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:6_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:7_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:8_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-7">[7]</a></sup> The Coca-Cola Company is the world's largest producer of plastic waste (frequently disposed of improperly by consumers), producing over 3 million tons of <a href="/wiki/Plastic" title="Plastic">plastic</a> packaging each year including 110 billion plastic bottles.<sup id="cite_ref-:9_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:10_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:11_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:11-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:12_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:13_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:13-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:14_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FY-1">[1]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Equity_(finance)" title="Equity (finance)">Total equity</a></span></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><img alt="Decrease" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$16.98 billion</span> <span style="font-size:85%;">(2018)</span><sup id="cite_ref-FY_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FY-1">[1]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Number of employees</div></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;">62,600 <span style="font-size:85%;">(2018)</span><sup id="cite_ref-FY_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FY-1">[1]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Subsidiary" title="Subsidiary">Subsidiaries</a></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><a href="/wiki/List_of_assets_owned_by_The_Coca-Cola_Company" title="List of assets owned by The Coca-Cola Company">List of The Coca-Cola Company subsidiaries</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://coca-colacompany.com/">Coca-ColaCompany.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table><p>The company—headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>, but incorporated in <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup>—has operated a <a href="/wiki/Franchising" title="Franchising">franchised</a> distribution system since 1889: the Company largely produces syrup concentrate, which is then sold to various <a href="/wiki/Bottling_company" title="Bottling company">bottlers</a> throughout the world who hold exclusive territories. The company owns its <a href="/wiki/Anchor_bottler" title="Anchor bottler">anchor bottler</a> in North America, <b>Coca-Cola Refreshments</b>.
The company's stock is listed on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">NYSE</a> and is part of <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average" title="Dow Jones Industrial Average">DJIA</a> and the <a href="/wiki/S%26P_500" class="mw-redirect" title="S&amp;P 500">S&amp;P 500</a> and <a href="/wiki/S%26P_100" title="S&amp;P 100">S&amp;P 100</a> indexes.
</p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a></div><p>In 1886, pharmacist John Pemberton from Columbus, Georgia invented the original Coca-Cola drink and sold it as a medicinal beverage.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-15">[15]</a></sup> Pemberton's bookkeeper, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Mason_Robinson" title="Frank Mason Robinson">Frank M. Robinson</a>, is credited with naming the product and creating its logo.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Robinson chose the name Coca-Cola because of its two main ingredients (coca leaves and kola nuts) and because it sounded like an alliteration. John Pemberton had taken a break and left Robinson to make and promote, as well as sell Coca-Cola on his own. He promoted the drink with the limited budget that he had and succeeded.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-17">[17]</a></sup></p><p>In 1889, American businessman Asa G. Candler completed his purchase of the Coca-Cola formula and brand from Pemberton's heirs.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:6_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:8_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-15">[15]</a></sup> In 1892, the Coca-Cola Company was formally founded in Atlanta by Candler.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:6_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:7_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:8_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-7">[7]</a></sup> By 1895, Coca-Cola was being sold in every state in the union.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-18">[18]</a></sup> In 1919, the company was sold to <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Woodruff" title="Ernest Woodruff">Ernest Woodruff</a>'s Trust Company of Georgia.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p><p>Coca-Cola's first ad read "Coca Cola. Delicious! Refreshing! Exhilarating! Invigorating!"<sup id="cite_ref-:3_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-17">[17]</a></sup> Candler was one of the first businessmen to use merchandising in his advertising strategy.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-15">[15]</a></sup> As of 1948, Coca-Cola had claimed about 60% of its market share.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-18">[18]</a></sup> By 1984, The Coca-Cola Company's market share decreased to 21.8% due to new competitors, namely <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisitions">Acquisitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Acquisitions" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The company has a long history of acquisitions. Coca-Cola acquired <a href="/wiki/Minute_Maid" title="Minute Maid">Minute Maid</a> in 1960<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> and in 1982, it acquired the movie studio <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Pictures" title="Columbia Pictures">Columbia Pictures</a> for $692 million but Columbia was sold to <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a> for $3 billion in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-sellers19971013_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sellers19971013-21">[21]</a></sup> It acquired the Indian cola brand <a href="/wiki/Thums_Up" title="Thums Up">Thums Up</a> in 1993,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Barq%27s" title="Barq's">Barq's</a> in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In 2001, it acquired the <a href="/wiki/Odwalla" title="Odwalla">Odwalla</a> brand of fruit juices, smoothies, and bars for $181 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Coca-Cola-Oct-2001-SC-TO-T_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coca-Cola-Oct-2001-SC-TO-T-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> In 2007, it acquired <a href="/wiki/Fuze_Beverage" title="Fuze Beverage">Fuze Beverage</a> from founder Lance Collins and Castanea Partners for an estimated $250 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Coca-Cola-Feb-2007-10-K_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coca-Cola-Feb-2007-10-K-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p><p>The company's 2009 bid to buy Chinese juice maker <a href="/wiki/Huiyuan_Juice" title="Huiyuan Juice">Huiyuan Juice Group</a> ended when China rejected its $2.4 billion bid, on the grounds the resulting company would be a virtual monopoly.<sup id="cite_ref-Coca-Cola-Apr-2009-10-Q_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coca-Cola-Apr-2009-10-Q-28">[28]</a></sup> Nationalism was also thought to be a reason for aborting the deal.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p><p>In 2011, it acquired the remaining stake in <a href="/wiki/Honest_Tea" title="Honest Tea">Honest Tea</a>, having bought a 40% stake in 2008 for $43m.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> In 2013, it finalized its purchase of <a href="/wiki/ZICO_(beverage)" title="ZICO (beverage)">ZICO</a>, a coconut water company.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> In August 2014, it acquired a 16.7% (currently 18.5% due to stock buy backs) stake in <a href="/wiki/Monster_Beverage" title="Monster Beverage">Monster Beverage</a> for $2.15 billion with an option to increase it to 25%, as part of a long-term strategic partnership that includes marketing and distribution alliance, and product line swap.<sup id="cite_ref-MonsterCoke_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MonsterCoke-34">[34]</a></sup> In 2015, the company took a minority stake ownership in the cold pressed juice manufacturer, Suja Life LLC.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> In December 2016, it bought many of the former <a href="/wiki/SABMiller" title="SABMiller">SABMiller</a>'s Coca-Cola operations.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The Coca-Cola Company owns a 68.3% stake in Coca-Cola Bottlers Africa.  Coca-Cola Bottlers Africa's headquarters located in Port Elizabeth South Africa.
</p><p>In 2017, The Coca-Cola Company acquired Mexican sparkling water brand Topo Chico.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p><p>On August 31, 2018, it agreed to acquire <a href="/wiki/Costa_Coffee" title="Costa Coffee">Costa Coffee</a> from <a href="/wiki/Whitbread" title="Whitbread">Whitbread</a> for £3.9bn. The acquisition closed on 3 January 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p><p>The Coca-Cola Company acquired a 40% stake in Chi Ltd on January 30, 2016. The Coca-Cola Company acquired the remaining 60% stake in Chi Ltd on January 30, 2019.
</p><p>During August 2018 The Coca-Cola Company acquired <a href="/wiki/Moxie" title="Moxie">Moxie</a> for an undisclosed amount.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p><p>On September 19, 2018 The Coca-Cola Company acquired Organic &amp; Raw Trading Co. Pty Ltd the manufacturer of MOJO Kombucha in Willunga, Australia.
</p><p>On August 14, 2018 The Coca-Cola Company announced a minority interest in Body Armor.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>On October 5, 2018 The Coca-Cola Company acquired a 22.5% stake in MADE Group from the company's 3 founders; Luke Marget, Matt Dennis and Brad Wilson.
The Coca-Cola Company owns a 30.8% stake in Coca-Cola Amatil ltd, therefore The Coca-Cola Company owns a further 6.93% stake in MADE Group through its ownership stake in Coca-Cola Amatil ltd.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Revenue_and_sales">Revenue and sales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Revenue and sales" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CocaColaSugarLandTX.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/CocaColaSugarLandTX.JPG/220px-CocaColaSugarLandTX.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="182" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2058" data-file-height="1703"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 182px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/CocaColaSugarLandTX.JPG/220px-CocaColaSugarLandTX.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="182" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CocaColaSugarLandTX.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Coca-Cola Company's Minute Maid group North America offices in <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Land_Town_Square" title="Sugar Land Town Square">Sugar Land Town Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Land,_Texas" title="Sugar Land, Texas">Sugar Land, Texas</a>, United States</div></div></div>
<p>According to The Coca-Cola Company's 2005 <a href="/wiki/Annual_Report" class="mw-redirect" title="Annual Report">Annual Report</a>, the firm at that time sold beverage products in more than 200 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-archivesa_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archivesa-41">[41]</a></sup> The 2005 report further states that of the more than 50 billion beverage servings of all types consumed worldwide, daily, beverages bearing the trademarks owned by or licensed to Coca-Cola account for approximately $1.5 billion. Of these, beverages bearing the trademark "<a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a>" or "Coke" accounted for approximately 78% of the company's total gallon sales.<sup id="cite_ref-archivesa_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archivesa-41">[41]</a></sup></p><p>In 2010, it was announced that Coca-Cola had become the first brand to top £1 billion in annual UK grocery sales.<sup id="cite_ref-Edinburgh_Evening_News_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Edinburgh_Evening_News-42">[42]</a></sup> In 2017, Coke sales were down 11% from a year earlier due to consumer tastes shifting away from sugary drinks and health risks associated with artificial sweeteners in diet drinks.<sup id="cite_ref-sales_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sales-43">[43]</a></sup></p>

</td></tr></tbody></table></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Stock">Stock</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Stock" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coca_Cola_1929.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Coca_Cola_1929.JPG/220px-Coca_Cola_1929.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3242" data-file-height="2463"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 167px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Coca_Cola_1929.JPG/220px-Coca_Cola_1929.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="167" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coca_Cola_1929.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Certificate of Purchase Class A Stock for 20 Shares of The Coca-Cola Company, issued 20. February 1929</div></div></div>
<p>Since 1919, Coca-Cola has been a publicly traded company.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Its stock is listed on the New York Stock Exchange under the ticker symbol "KO".<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> One share of stock purchased in 1919 for $40, with all dividends reinvested, would have been worth $9.8 million in 2012, a 10.7% annual increase adjusted for inflation.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> A predecessor bank of <a href="/wiki/SunTrust" class="mw-redirect" title="SunTrust">SunTrust</a> received $100,000 for underwriting Coca-Cola's 1919 public offering; the bank sold that stock for over $2 billion in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> In 1987, Coca-Cola once again became one of the 30 stocks which makes up the <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average" title="Dow Jones Industrial Average">Dow Jones Industrial Average</a>, which is commonly referenced as a proxy for stock market performance; it had previously been a Dow stock from 1932 to 1935.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Coca-Cola has paid a dividend since 1920 and (as of 2019) has increased it each year for 57 years.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Stock is available from a <a href="/wiki/Dividend_reinvestment_plan" title="Dividend reinvestment plan">direct purchase program</a>, through <a href="/wiki/Computershare_Trust_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Computershare Trust Company">Computershare Trust Company</a>, but unlike many programs, has investment fees.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Staff_and_management">Staff and management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Staff and management" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main page: <a href="/wiki/Category:Coca-Cola_people" title="Category:Coca-Cola people">Category:Coca-Cola people</a></div>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Bottlers">Bottlers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Bottlers" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a href="/wiki/File:15-09-26-RalfR-WLC-0098.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/15-09-26-RalfR-WLC-0098.jpg/100px-15-09-26-RalfR-WLC-0098.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="177" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2354" data-file-height="4174"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 100px;height: 177px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/15-09-26-RalfR-WLC-0098.jpg/100px-15-09-26-RalfR-WLC-0098.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="100" data-height="177" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:15-09-26-RalfR-WLC-0098.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coca-Cola</div></div></div>
<p>In general, The Coca-Cola Company and its <a href="/wiki/Subsidiaries" class="mw-redirect" title="Subsidiaries">subsidiaries</a> only produce <a href="/wiki/Syrup" title="Syrup">syrup</a> concentrate, which is then sold to various <a href="/wiki/Bottling_company" title="Bottling company">bottlers</a> throughout the world who hold a local Coca-Cola <a href="/wiki/Franchising" title="Franchising">franchise</a>. Coca-Cola bottlers, who hold territorially exclusive contracts with the company, produce the finished product in cans and bottles from the concentrate, in combination with filtered water and sweeteners. The bottlers then sell, distribute, and merchandise the resulting Coca-Cola product to <a href="/wiki/Retail_store" class="mw-redirect" title="Retail store">retail stores</a>, vending machines, restaurants, and food service distributors. Outside the United States, these bottlers also control the fountain business.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>Since the early 1980s, the company has actively encouraged the consolidation of bottlers, with the company often owning a share of these "anchor bottlers".<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<dl><dt>Outside North America</dt></dl><p>The company's largest bottlers outside North America are:<sup id="cite_ref-largest_bottlers_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-largest_bottlers-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Amatil" title="Coca-Cola Amatil">Coca-Cola Amatil</a>, based in Australia (Australia, New Zealand, Indonesia, South Pacific nations) (Company owns 30.8%)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_European_Partners" title="Coca-Cola European Partners">Coca-Cola European Partners PLC</a>, based in the United Kingdom (western Europe) (Company owns 18.1%)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/International_Beverages_Pvt._Ltd." class="mw-redirect" title="International Beverages Pvt. Ltd.">International Beverages Pvt. Ltd.</a>, based in Bangladesh (Fully owned subsidiary of The Coca-Cola Company)<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Bottling_Shqip%C3%ABria" title="Coca-Cola Bottling Shqipëria">Coca-Cola Bottling Shqipëria</a>, based in Albania</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Bottlers_Philippines,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Coca-Cola Bottlers Philippines, Inc.">Coca-Cola Bottlers Philippines, Inc.</a>, based in the Philippines (Fully owned subsidiary of The Coca-Cola Company)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_FEMSA" title="Coca-Cola FEMSA">Coca-Cola FEMSA</a>, based in Mexico (parts of Mexico and Latin America) (Company owns 27.8%)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arca_Continental" title="Arca Continental">Arca Continental</a>, also based in Mexico (parts of Mexico and Latin America and in US under Coca-Cola Southwest Beverages LLC in the state of Texas and parts of New Mexico, Oklahoma and Arkansas ) (independent)</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Embotelladora_Andina_S.A&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Embotelladora Andina S.A (page does not exist)">Embotelladora Andina S.A</a>, based in Chile (southern South America) (Company owns 14.7% of series A common stock outstanding &amp; 14.7% of series B common stock outstanding)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Beverages_Africa" title="Coca-Cola Beverages Africa">Coca-Cola Beverages Africa</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Port_Elizabeth,_South_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Port Elizabeth, South Africa">Port Elizabeth, South Africa</a> (southern and eastern Africa) (company owns 68.3%)</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Coca-Cola_Korea&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Coca-Cola Korea (page does not exist)">Coca-Cola Korea</a>, based in South Korea (independent)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_HBC_AG" class="mw-redirect" title="Coca-Cola HBC AG">Coca-Cola HBC AG</a>, originally based in Greece but now located in Switzerland (Greece, Ireland, Eastern Europe, Russia, and Nigeria)    (Company owns 23.2%)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Icecek" class="mw-redirect" title="Coca-Cola Icecek">Coca-Cola Icecek</a> Based in Turkey (Turkey, South West Asia, Arabia) (Company owns 20.1%)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Swire_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Swire Group">Swire Group</a>, based in Hong Kong (China, Taiwan, Hong Kong) (independent)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kirin_Company" title="Kirin Company">Kirin Company</a>, based in Japan (independent)</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Coca-Cola_Japan_Holdings&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Coca-Cola Japan Holdings (page does not exist)">Coca-Cola Japan Holdings</a> (Company owns 16.3%)</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=PT_Coca-Cola_Bottling_Indonesia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="PT Coca-Cola Bottling Indonesia (page does not exist)">PT Coca-Cola Bottling Indonesia</a> (Company owns 29.4%)  (Coca-Cola Amatil ltd owns 70.6%)</li></ul><dl><dt>In the United States</dt></dl><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CocaColaBottlingHouston.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/CocaColaBottlingHouston.JPG/200px-CocaColaBottlingHouston.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 150px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/CocaColaBottlingHouston.JPG/200px-CocaColaBottlingHouston.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="150" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CocaColaBottlingHouston.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Houston Coca-Cola Bottling Company</div></div></div>
<p>In the United States, the company bypasses bottlers and is responsible for the manufacture and sale of fountain syrups directly to authorized fountain wholesalers and some fountain retailers.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p><p>After purchasing the North American assets of <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Enterprises" title="Coca-Cola Enterprises">Coca-Cola Enterprises</a>, as of 2014 the company directly owns 100% of Coca-Cola Refreshments, the anchor bottler of Coca-Cola products in North America, representing about 90% of Canada and 80% of the United States.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>Other major bottlers in the United States are:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Bottling_Co._Consolidated" title="Coca-Cola Bottling Co. Consolidated">Coca-Cola Bottling Co. Consolidated</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte, North Carolina</a> (company owns 34.8%)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Beverages_Northeast" title="Coca-Cola Beverages Northeast">Coca-Cola Beverages Northeast</a> based in <a href="/wiki/Bedford,_New_Hampshire" title="Bedford, New Hampshire">Bedford, New Hampshire</a> and owned by Kirin Company</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Bottling_Company_United" title="Coca-Cola Bottling Company United">Coca-Cola Bottling Company United</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Birmingham,_Alabama" title="Birmingham, Alabama">Birmingham, Alabama</a> (independent)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Swire_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Swire Group">Swire Coca-Cola USA</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City" title="Salt Lake City">Salt Lake City</a>, Utah and owned by Swire Group</li></ul><p>In September 2015, the company announced the sale of several production plants and territories to Swire, Consolidated, and United, and creation of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coca-Cola_National_Product_Supply_System&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Coca-Cola National Product Supply System (page does not exist)">Coca-Cola National Product Supply System</a> which controls 95% of the territory in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Consumer_relations_and_civic_involvement">Consumer relations and civic involvement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Consumer relations and civic involvement" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<p>After <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Martin Luther King, Jr.">Martin Luther King, Jr.</a> won the 1964 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a>, plans for an interracial celebratory dinner in still-<a href="/wiki/Segregated_Atlanta" class="mw-redirect" title="Segregated Atlanta">segregated Atlanta</a> were not initially well supported by the city's business elite until Coca-Cola intervened.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p><a href="/wiki/J._Paul_Austin" title="J. Paul Austin">J. Paul Austin</a>, the chairman and CEO of Coca-Cola, and Mayor Ivan Allen summoned key Atlanta business leaders to the Commerce Club's eighteenth floor dining room, where Austin told them flatly, 'It is embarrassing for Coca-Cola to be located in a city that refuses to honor its Nobel Prize winner. We are an international business. The Coca-Cola Company does not need Atlanta. You all need to decide whether Atlanta needs the Coca-Cola Company.' Within two hours of the end of that meeting, every ticket to the dinner was sold.</p><div class="templatequotecite">— <cite><a href="/wiki/Andrew_Young" title="Andrew Young">Andrew Young</a><sup id="cite_ref-Young_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Young-76">[76]</a></sup></cite></div></blockquote>
<p>Throughout 2012, Coca-Cola contributed $1,700,500 to a $46 million political campaign known as "The Coalition Against The Costly Food Labeling Proposition, sponsored by Farmers and Food Producers".<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> This organization was set up to oppose a citizen's initiative, known as Proposition 37, demanding mandatory labeling of foods containing genetically modified ingredients.<sup id="cite_ref-Prop_37_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prop_37-78">[78]</a></sup></p><p>In 2012, Coca-Cola was listed as a partner of the <a href="/wiki/Product_Red" title="Product Red">(RED)</a> campaign, together with other brands such as <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc" class="mw-redirect" title="Nike, Inc">Nike</a>, <a href="/wiki/Girl_Distribution_Company" title="Girl Distribution Company">Girl</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Express" title="American Express">American Express</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Converse_(shoe_company)" title="Converse (shoe company)">Converse</a>. The campaign's mission is to prevent the transmission of the <a href="/wiki/Human_immunodeficiency_virus" class="mw-redirect" title="Human immunodeficiency virus">HIV virus</a> from mother to child by 2015 (the campaign's byline is "Fighting for an AIDS Free Generation").<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Plastic_production_and_waste">Plastic production and waste</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Plastic production and waste" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed"><li class="gallerybox" style="width: 154px"><div style="width: 154px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 152px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coca_Cola_plastic_bottles.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Coca_Cola_plastic_bottles.jpg/228px-Coca_Cola_plastic_bottles.jpg" decoding="async" width="152" height="120" data-file-width="3849" data-file-height="3042"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 152px;height: 120px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Coca_Cola_plastic_bottles.jpg/228px-Coca_Cola_plastic_bottles.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="152" data-height="120"> </span></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Coca-Cola bottles as <a href="/wiki/Plastic_debris" class="mw-redirect" title="Plastic debris">pollution in water</a>
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 215.33333333333px"><div style="width: 215.33333333333px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 213.33333333333px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><div id="mwe_player_0" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:214px;" videopayload='&lt;div class="mediaContainer" style="width:854px"&gt;&lt;video id="mwe_player_1" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Transforming_the_Plastics_Economy.webm/854px--Transforming_the_Plastics_Economy.webm.jpg" controls="" preload="none" autoplay="" style="width:854px;height:480px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="3704.542" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Transforming_the_Plastics_Economy.webm" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/f/f7/Transforming_the_Plastics_Economy.webm/Transforming_the_Plastics_Economy.webm.480p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm;
