			<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Discussion about plastic waste with the Coca-Cola CEO
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul><p>The Coca-Cola Company is the world's largest producer of plastic waste (frequently disposed of improperly by consumers), for two years in a row<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> producing over 3 million tonnes of <a href="/wiki/Plastic" title="Plastic">plastic</a> packaging each year including 110 billion plastic bottles.<sup id="cite_ref-:9_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:10_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:11_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:11-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:12_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:13_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:13-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:14_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:14-13">[13]</a></sup> The company's global chief executive has admitted that Coca-Cola has no plans to reduce its use of plastic bottles;<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> in fact, the company has "quietly fought efforts" to reduce the amount of plastic waste it creates, partly by opposing <a href="/wiki/Bottle_Bill" class="mw-redirect" title="Bottle Bill">bottle bill</a> legislation.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> The head of sustainability Bea Perez has said they will continue to use plastic, claiming "customers like them because they reseal and are lightweight".<sup id="cite_ref-:8_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-7">[7]</a></sup> There are studies which show that 80% of customers are aiming to reduce their contribution to plastic waste, 69% are willing to pay more for eco-friendly packaging, and most support a ban on harmful plastic packaging.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Criticism" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Coca-Cola" title="Criticism of Coca-Cola">Criticism of Coca-Cola</a></div>
<p>Since the early 2000s, the criticisms over the use of Coca-Cola products as well as the company itself, escalated with concerns over health effects, environmental issues, <a href="/wiki/Animal_testing" title="Animal testing">animal testing</a>, economic business practices and employee issues. The Coca-Cola Company has been faced with multiple lawsuits concerning these various criticisms.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Advertising">Advertising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Advertising" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%2796-%2702_Chevrolet_Express_Wagon_Coca-Cola.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/%2796-%2702_Chevrolet_Express_Wagon_Coca-Cola.jpg/200px-%2796-%2702_Chevrolet_Express_Wagon_Coca-Cola.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="134" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2086" data-file-height="1401"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 134px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/%2796-%2702_Chevrolet_Express_Wagon_Coca-Cola.jpg/200px-%2796-%2702_Chevrolet_Express_Wagon_Coca-Cola.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="134" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%2796-%2702_Chevrolet_Express_Wagon_Coca-Cola.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Express" title="Chevrolet Express">Chevrolet Express</a> van bearing the logo of The Coca-Cola Company.</div></div></div>
<p>Coca-Cola advertising has "been among the most prolific in marketing history", with a notable and major impact on popular culture and society as a whole.
</p><p>The logo, bottle design, and brand image are internationally recognizable. Their product is ranked the number one soft drink, repeatedly, internationally, and has notoriety as the first soft drink consumed by astronauts in space. Coca-Cola employs a diverse range of integrated marketing communications to advertise through direct marketing, web based media, social media, and sales promotions (Stringer, 2015).<sup id="cite_ref-:0_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-85">[85]</a></sup></p><p>The company carefully considers all touch points a consumer (or prospective consumer) has with the brand as potential delivery channels for the brand's message, and makes use of all relevant communication systems. This well established, long-standing, consistent approach has created a longing for the product that by far "superseded the desire for that typically associated with a drink to quench one's thirst" (Dudovskiy, 2015).<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<dl><dt>Direct marketing</dt></dl><p>They have exclusive vendor company partnerships, which eliminates competition, e.g. cinemas and <a href="/wiki/Restaurants" class="mw-redirect" title="Restaurants">restaurants</a> only serving Coca-Cola over <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a>. At sponsored sporting events, they again eliminate competition by attaining sole sale rights as well as VIP sales opportunities to important clients, for example, <a href="/wiki/Baseball_field" title="Baseball field">baseball fields</a>.
</p>
<dl><dt>Viral marketing</dt></dl><p>The company also markets via mobile marketing in text messages, e.g. viral marketing campaigns (Stringer, 2015).<sup id="cite_ref-:0_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<dl><dt>Web and social media</dt></dl><p>They set the industry benchmark as the brand so universally recognized that audience building is unnecessary. Their fan engagement spans 86 million globally across social media channels. They deliver a consistently unified message whether it be through new products, online interaction, and social, cultural, or sporting events (Stringer, 2015).<sup id="cite_ref-:0_85-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<dl><dt>Sales and promotions</dt></dl><p>In the retail setting, direct store beverage delivery trucks (mobile advertising) as well as point of sale coolers and vending machines have bright red logo blazoned branding. In terms of food service, Coca-Cola is a food pairing suggestion that is now ingrained as a food match, e.g., for popcorn, burgers, fries, and hot dog combos (Stringer, 2015).<sup id="cite_ref-:0_85-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(10)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Products_and_brands">Products and brands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Products and brands" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-10 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-10">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Coca-Cola_brands" title="List of Coca-Cola brands">List of Coca-Cola brands</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_assets_owned_by_The_Coca-Cola_Company" title="List of assets owned by The Coca-Cola Company">List of assets owned by The Coca-Cola Company</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coca-Cola_offices_(Madrid,_Spain)_04.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Coca-Cola_offices_%28Madrid%2C_Spain%29_04.jpg/220px-Coca-Cola_offices_%28Madrid%2C_Spain%29_04.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2391" data-file-height="1425"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 131px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Coca-Cola_offices_%28Madrid%2C_Spain%29_04.jpg/220px-Coca-Cola_offices_%28Madrid%2C_Spain%29_04.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="131" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coca-Cola_offices_(Madrid,_Spain)_04.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coca-Cola Company's office building in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> (Spain)</div></div></div>
<p>The Coca-Cola Company offers more than 350 brands in over 200 countries, aside from its namesake <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> beverage.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-food_assets">Non-food assets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Non-food assets" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<h4 class="in-block"><span id="Columbia_Pictures_.28no_longer_owned.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Columbia_Pictures_(no_longer_owned)">Columbia Pictures (no longer owned)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Columbia Pictures (no longer owned)" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Coca-Cola bought <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Pictures" title="Columbia Pictures">Columbia Pictures</a> in 1982, owing to the low monetary value of the studio. The film company was the first and only studio ever owned by Coca-Cola. During its ownership of the studio, Columbia released many popular films including <i><a href="/wiki/Ghostbusters" title="Ghostbusters">Ghostbusters</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Stripes_(film)" title="Stripes (film)">Stripes</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Karate_Kid_(1984_film)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Karate Kid (1984 film)">The Karate Kid</a></i>, and some others. However, two years after the critical and commercial failure of the 1987 film <i><a href="/wiki/Ishtar_(film)" title="Ishtar (film)">Ishtar</a></i>, Columbia was spun-off and then sold to <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a> in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-sellers19971013_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sellers19971013-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="World_of_Coca-Cola">World of Coca-Cola</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: World of Coca-Cola" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/World_of_Coca-Cola" title="World of Coca-Cola">World of Coca-Cola</a></div>
<p>Coca-Cola operates a soft drink themed tourist attraction in Atlanta, Georgia; the <a href="/wiki/World_of_Coca-Cola" title="World of Coca-Cola">World of Coca-Cola</a> is a multi-storied exhibition. It features flavor sampling and a history museum, with locations in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Vegas, Nevada">Las Vegas, Nevada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Buena_Vista,_Florida" title="Lake Buena Vista, Florida">Lake Buena Vista, Florida</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_of_Coca-Cola_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_of_Coca-Cola-87">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rolling_Out_-_World_of_Coca-Cola_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Out_-_World_of_Coca-Cola-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Brands">Brands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Brands" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_soft_drinks">Other soft drinks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Other soft drinks" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>The Coca-Cola Company also produces a number of other soft drinks including <a href="/wiki/Fanta" title="Fanta">Fanta</a> (introduced circa 1941) and <a href="/wiki/Sprite_(soft_drink)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sprite (soft drink)">Sprite</a>. Fanta's origins date back to World War II during a trade embargo against Germany on cola syrup, making it impossible to sell Coca-Cola in Germany. <a href="/wiki/Max_Keith" title="Max Keith">Max Keith</a>, the head of Coca-Cola's German office during the war, decided to create a new product for the German market, made only from products available in Germany at the time, which they named Fanta.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> The drink proved to be a hit, and when Coke took over again after the war, it adopted the Fanta brand as well. Fanta was originally an orange flavored soft drink which can come in <a href="/wiki/Plastic_bottle" title="Plastic bottle">plastic bottles</a> or cans. It has become available in many different flavors now such as grape, peach, grapefruit, apple, pineapple, and strawberry.
</p><p>In 1961, Coca-Cola introduced Sprite, a lemon-lime soft drink, and another of the company's bestsellers and its response to <a href="/wiki/7_Up" title="7 Up">7 Up</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tab_(soft_drink)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tab (soft drink)">Tab</a> was Coca-Cola's first attempt to develop a diet soft drink, using <a href="/wiki/Saccharin" title="Saccharin">saccharin</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Sugar_substitute" title="Sugar substitute">sugar substitute</a>. Introduced in 1963, the product is still sold today, although its sales have dwindled since the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Diet_Coke" title="Diet Coke">Diet Coke</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tab_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tab-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Last_Minute_Refreshment.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Last_Minute_Refreshment.jpg/220px-Last_Minute_Refreshment.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 293px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Last_Minute_Refreshment.jpg/220px-Last_Minute_Refreshment.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="293" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Last_Minute_Refreshment.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An ad in Berlin, Germany.</div></div></div>
<p>Coca-Cola South Africa also released <a href="/wiki/Valpre" title="Valpre">Valpre</a> Bottled "still" and "sparkling" water.
</p><p>In 1969, the company released Simba, which was a take on Mountain Dew, and had packaging that was African desert themed, replete with an African Lion as the symbol of the brand.  The tagline was "Simba – It Conquers the African Thirst."
</p><p>Also in 1969, the company released a line of products under the name of Santiba, which was targeted for mixing cocktails and party usage, products including Quinine water and Ginger Ale.  Like the above-mentioned Simba, the Santiba line of products was short lived in the marketplace.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="BreakMate">BreakMate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: BreakMate" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/BreakMate" title="BreakMate">BreakMate</a></div>
<p>No longer manufactured, the Coca-Cola BreakMate was a three-flavor dispenser introduced by Coca-Cola and <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> in 1988. Intended for use in offices with five to fifty people,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> its refrigerated compartment held three individual one-litre plastic containers of soda syrup and a CO<sub>2</sub> tank. Like a soda fountain, it mixed syrup in a 1:5 ratio with carbonated water. In North America, Coca-Cola discontinued spare BreakMate parts in 2007 and stopped distributing the syrup in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthy_beverages">Healthy beverages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Healthy beverages" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>During the 1990s, the company responded to the growing consumer interest in healthy beverages by introducing several new non-carbonated beverage brands. These included <a href="/wiki/Minute_Maid" title="Minute Maid">Minute Maid</a> Juices to Go, <a href="/wiki/Powerade" title="Powerade">Powerade</a> sports beverage, flavored tea <a href="/wiki/Nestea" title="Nestea">Nestea</a> (in a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9" title="Nestlé">Nestlé</a>), <a href="/wiki/Fruitopia" title="Fruitopia">Fruitopia</a> fruit drink, and <a href="/wiki/Dasani" title="Dasani">Dasani</a> water, among others. In 2001, the Minute Maid division launched the <a href="/wiki/Simply_Orange" class="mw-redirect" title="Simply Orange">Simply Orange</a> brand of juices including <a href="/wiki/Orange_juice" title="Orange juice">orange juice</a>. In 2016, <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_India" title="Coca-Cola India">Coca-Cola India</a> introduced <a href="/wiki/Vio_(flavoured_milk)" title="Vio (flavoured milk)">Vio</a> to enter into the value-added <a href="/wiki/Dairy_product" title="Dairy product">dairy</a> category. The product lays the foundation for Coca-Cola's new segment after <a href="/wiki/Soft_drink" title="Soft drink">carbonated beverages</a>, water and juices.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p><p>In 2004, perhaps in response to the burgeoning popularity of <a href="/wiki/Low-carbohydrate_diet" title="Low-carbohydrate diet">low-carbohydrate diets</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Atkins_diet" title="Atkins diet">Atkins diet</a>, Coca-Cola announced its intention to develop and sell a low-carbohydrate alternative to Coke Classic, dubbed <a href="/wiki/C2_Cola" class="mw-redirect" title="C2 Cola">C2 Cola</a>. C2 contains a mix of <a href="/wiki/High_fructose_corn_syrup" class="mw-redirect" title="High fructose corn syrup">high fructose corn syrup</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aspartame" title="Aspartame">aspartame</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sucralose" title="Sucralose">sucralose</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Acesulfame_potassium" title="Acesulfame potassium">Acesulfame potassium</a>. C2 is designed to more closely emulate the taste of Coca-Cola Classic. Even with less than half of the <a href="/wiki/Food_energy" title="Food energy">food energy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carbohydrate" title="Carbohydrate">carbohydrates</a> of standard soft drinks, C2 is not a replacement for zero-calorie soft drinks such as Diet Coke. C2 went on sale in the U.S. on June 11, 2004, and in Canada in August 2004. C2's future is uncertain due to disappointing sales.
</p><p>Starting in 2009, The Coca-Cola Company invested in <a href="/wiki/Innocent_Drinks" title="Innocent Drinks">Innocent Drinks</a>, first with a minor stake, increasing to 90% in the first quarter of 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-ccc_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ccc-94">[94]</a></sup></p><p>It was in May 2014 when Finley, a sparkling fruit-flavored drink, was launched in France. It was launched in other countries later,<sup id="cite_ref-aaa_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aaa-95">[95]</a></sup> including Belgium and Luxembourg in September 2014. Coca-Cola first started developing the drink in Belgium in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-bbb_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbb-96">[96]</a></sup> As of 2014, the drink is targeted for adults, and is low in sugar with four flavors.<sup id="cite_ref-aaa_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aaa-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Best_selling">Best selling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Best selling" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Coca-Cola is the best-selling soft drink in most countries, and was recognized as the number one global brand in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> While the Middle East is one of the only regions in the world where Coca-Cola is not the number one soda drink, Coca-Cola nonetheless holds almost 25% market share (to Pepsi's 75%) and had double-digit growth in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Similarly, in Scotland, where the locally produced <a href="/wiki/Irn-Bru" title="Irn-Bru">Irn-Bru</a> was once more popular, 2005 figures show that both Coca-Cola and Diet Coke now outsell Irn-Bru.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> In Peru, the native <a href="/wiki/Inca_Kola" title="Inca Kola">Inca Kola</a> has been more popular than Coca-Cola, which prompted Coca-Cola to enter in negotiations with the soft drink's company and buy 50% of its stakes. In Japan, the best selling soft drink is not cola, as (canned) <a href="/wiki/Canned_tea" title="Canned tea">tea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_canned_coffee" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese canned coffee">coffee</a> are more popular.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> As such, The Coca-Cola Company's best selling brand there is not Coca-Cola, but <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(drink)" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgia (drink)">Georgia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> In May 2016, The Coca-Cola Company temporarily halted production of its signature drink in Venezuela due to sugar shortages.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Since then, The Coca-Cola Company has been using "minimum inventories of raw material" to make their signature drinks at two production plants in Venezuela.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Information">Information</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Information" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>On July 6, 2006, a Coca-Cola employee and two other people were arrested and charged with trying to sell trade secret information to the soft drink maker's competitor <a href="/wiki/PepsiCo" title="PepsiCo">PepsiCo</a> for $1.5 million. The recipe for Coca-Cola, perhaps the company's most closely guarded secret, was never in jeopardy; instead, the information was related to a new beverage in development. Coca-Cola executives verified that the trade secret documents in question were genuine and proprietary to the company. At least one glass vial containing a sample of a new drink was offered for sale, court documents said. The conspiracy was revealed by PepsiCo, which notified authorities when it was approached by the conspirators.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_tea">Green tea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Green tea" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>The company announced a new "negative <a href="/wiki/Calorie" title="Calorie">calorie</a>" green tea drink, <a href="/wiki/Enviga" title="Enviga">Enviga</a>, in 2006, along with trying coffee retail concepts <a href="/wiki/Far_Coast" title="Far Coast">Far Coast</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chaqwa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Chaqwa (page does not exist)">Chaqwa</a>.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Glaceau">Glaceau</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Glaceau" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>On May 25, 2007, Coca-Cola announced it would purchase <a href="/wiki/Glaceau" class="mw-redirect" title="Glaceau">Glaceau</a>, a maker of flavored vitamin-enhanced drinks (vitamin water), flavored waters, and <a href="/wiki/Burn_(energy_drink)" title="Burn (energy drink)">Burn</a> energy drinks, for $4.1 billion in cash.<sup id="cite_ref-TCCC-Glaceau_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCCC-Glaceau-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Huiyuan_Juice">Huiyuan Juice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Huiyuan Juice" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>On September 3, 2008, Coca-Cola announced its intention to make cash offers to purchase <a href="/wiki/Huiyuan_Juice" title="Huiyuan Juice">China Huiyuan Juice Group Limited</a> (which had a 42% share of the Chinese pure fruit juice market<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup>) for US$2.4bn (HK$12.20 per share).<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> China's <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Commerce_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Commerce of the People's Republic of China">ministry of commerce</a> blocked the deal on March 18, 2009, arguing that the deal would hurt small local juice companies, could have pushed up juice market prices, and limited consumers' choices.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Coke_Mini_can">Coke Mini can</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Coke Mini can" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In October 2009, Coca-Cola revealed its new 90-calorie <a href="/wiki/Coke_mini" class="mw-redirect" title="Coke mini">mini can</a> that holds 7.5 fluid ounces.<sup id="cite_ref-cokemini_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cokemini-109">[109]</a></sup> The mini can is often sold in 8 packs. Despite costing nearly 30 percent more per ounce, the mini cans have been met with positive sales figures.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Holiday_can">Holiday can</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Holiday can" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In November 2011, Coca-Cola revealed a seasonal design for their regular Coke cans as part of a partnership with the <a href="/wiki/World_Wild_Fund_for_Nature" class="mw-redirect" title="World Wild Fund for Nature">World Wildlife Fund</a>. However it was withdrawn only a month after release due to consumer complaints about the similar look to the silver cans commonly used for Diet Coke. There were also complaints about deviating from traditional red as the color of Coca-Cola cans previously.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Stake_in_Monster_Beverage">Stake in Monster Beverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Stake in Monster Beverage" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>It was announced on August 14, 2014, that Coca-Cola Co is making a cash payment of $2.15 billion for a 16.7 percent stake in <a href="/wiki/Monster_Beverage_Corp" class="mw-redirect" title="Monster Beverage Corp">Monster Beverage Corp</a> to expand its market for energy drinks. Coke's ownership in <a href="/wiki/Full_Throttle_(drink)" title="Full Throttle (drink)">Full Throttle</a> and Burn will be transferred to Monster. In return, Monster will transfer its ownership in <a href="/wiki/Hansen_Natural" class="mw-redirect" title="Hansen Natural">Hansen's Natural Sodas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peace_Iced_Tea" title="Peace Iced Tea">Peace Iced Tea</a> and Blue Sky Soda to The Coca-Cola Company. <a href="/wiki/Muhtar_Kent" title="Muhtar Kent">Muhtar Kent</a>, Coke's former chief executive officer, stated that the company has the option to increase its stake to 25 percent but cannot exceed that percentage in the next four years.<sup id="cite_ref-ATHAVALEY-Monster_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ATHAVALEY-Monster-112">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gelles-Monster_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gelles-Monster-113">[113]</a></sup>
Due to share buy backs by the board of directors of Monster Beverage Corporation, The Coca-Cola Company's stake has since increased to 18.5%.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(11)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorship">Sponsorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sponsorship" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-11 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-11">
<p>Coca-Cola's advertising expenses accounted for US$3.256 billion in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Sports" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Coca-Cola sponsored the <a href="/wiki/The_Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="The Football League">English Football League</a> from the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_in_English_football" title="2004–05 in English football">2004–05 season</a> (beginning August 2004) to the start of 2010/11 season, when the <a href="/wiki/Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League">Football League</a> replaced it with <a href="/wiki/Npower_(United_Kingdom)" title="Npower (United Kingdom)">NPower</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Along with this, Coca-Cola sponsored the Coca-Cola Football Camp, that took place in Pretoria, South Africa during the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a>, during which hundreds of teenagers from around the world were able to come together and share their love of the game, partly due to <a href="/wiki/Best_Buy" title="Best Buy">Best Buy</a>'s efforts through their @15 program.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p><p>Other major sponsorships include the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Football_League" title="Australian Football League">AFL</a>, <a href="/wiki/NHRA" class="mw-redirect" title="NHRA">NHRA</a>, <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a>, the <a href="/wiki/PGA_Tour" title="PGA Tour">PGA Tour</a>, <a href="/wiki/NCAA" class="mw-redirect" title="NCAA">NCAA</a> Championships, the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a>, the <a href="/wiki/NRL" class="mw-redirect" title="NRL">NRL</a>, the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cups</a> and the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA European Championships">UEFA European Championships</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The company partnered with <a href="/wiki/Panini_Group" title="Panini Group">Panini</a> to produce the first virtual sticker album for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a>, and they have collaborated for every World Cup since.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Each fall, Coca-Cola is the sponsor of the <a href="/wiki/TOUR_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="TOUR Championship">TOUR Championship</a> by Coca-Cola held at the <a href="/wiki/East_Lake_Golf_Club" title="East Lake Golf Club">East Lake Golf Club</a> in Atlanta, Georgia. The Tour Championship is the season ending tournament of the PGA Tour.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the Philippines, it has a team in the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Basketball_Association" title="Philippine Basketball Association">Philippine Basketball Association</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Powerade_Tigers" title="Powerade Tigers">Powerade Tigers</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>Since the season of 2019 is the title sponsor of the <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan_Super_League" title="Uzbekistan Super League">Uzbekistan Super League</a> in <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, and this league is officially called <i>Coca-Cola Uzbekistan Super League</i>.
Coca-Cola has also sponsored the Overwatch league since season two. They also sponsor all major Overwatch tournaments such as the world cup
.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> In February 2020, Coca-Cola became the title sponsor for the eNASCAR iRacing series.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Television" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The company sponsored the popular <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a> singing-competition series <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i> from 2002 until 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p><p>Coca-Cola was a sponsor of the nightly talk show on <a href="/wiki/PBS" title="PBS">PBS</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Charlie_Rose,_LLC" class="mw-redirect" title="Charlie Rose, LLC">Charlie Rose</a></i> in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p><p>Coca-Cola is also executive producers of <a href="/wiki/Coke_Studio_(Pakistan)" class="mw-redirect" title="Coke Studio (Pakistan)">Coke Studio (Pakistan)</a>. It was a franchising that started in Brazil, broadcast by <a href="/wiki/MTV_Brasil" title="MTV Brasil">MTV Brasil</a> and there are various adaptations of Coke Studio such as <a href="/wiki/Coke_Studio_(India)" class="mw-redirect" title="Coke Studio (India)">Coke Studio (India)</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coke_Studio_(Africa)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Coke Studio (Africa) (page does not exist)">Coke Studio (Africa)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Theme_parks">Theme parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Theme parks" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>While not necessarily having naming rights to anything in all locations, the company does sponsor and provide beverages in many theme parks, usually in an exclusive capacity. This includes the <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Parks_and_Resorts" class="mw-redirect" title="Walt Disney Parks and Resorts">Walt Disney Parks and Resorts</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[a]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Merlin_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="Merlin Entertainment">Merlin Entertainment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Universal_Parks_%26_Resorts" title="Universal Parks &amp; Resorts">Universal Parks &amp; Resorts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Six_Flags" title="Six Flags">Six Flags</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cedar_Fair" title="Cedar Fair">Cedar Fair</a>, and <a href="/wiki/SeaWorld_Entertainment" class="mw-redirect" title="SeaWorld Entertainment">SeaWorld Entertainment</a> which are six of the nine largest theme park operators worldwide (it is unknown whether OCT Parks China, the Chimelong Group, or Fantawild, the fourth, seventh, and eighth largest theme park operators respectively, use Coca-Cola).<sup id="cite_ref-2015_Report_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015_Report-126">[125]</a></sup></p><p>The company also directly sponsors, with naming rights, the Coca-Cola <a href="/wiki/London_Eye" title="London Eye">London Eye</a> and the Coca-Cola <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Eye" class="mw-redirect" title="Orlando Eye">Orlando Eye</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Orlando_Eye_1_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Orlando_Eye_1-127">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Orlando_Eye_2_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Orlando_Eye_2-128">[127]</a></sup></p><p>The company also operates "Coca-Cola" visitor centers in Israel, Belgium and Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-cafe.themarker.com_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cafe.themarker.com-129">[128]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mefik.co.il_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mefik.co.il-130">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(12)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: See also" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-12 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-12">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_assets_owned_by_The_Coca-Cola_Company" title="List of assets owned by The Coca-Cola Company">List of assets owned by The Coca-Cola Company</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stepan_Company" title="Stepan Company">Stepan Company</a> – produces coca leaf extract</li></ul></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(13)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: References" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-13 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-13">
